Calixarenes are a prominent class of macrocyclic compounds widely used as host molecules in supramolecular chemistry due to their tunable cavity sizes and versatile functionalization. Chemists have synthesized calixarene derivatives where pyrrole rings are introduced either at the upper or lower rim, or as bridging units between phenolic subunits. These pyrrole-functionalized calixarenes can exhibit enhanced binding properties for specific guest molecules, such as cations, anions, or neutral species, due to the additional hydrogen bonding and π-interactions provided by the pyrrole moieties. Such derivatives have been explored for applications in molecular recognition, sensing, and catalysis. Examples include calix[4]arenes with pyrrole groups appended at the para positions, or calixpyrroles, where the macrocycle itself is constructed from alternating phenol and pyrrole units.
